			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">2015 Southeast Asian haze</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<tr>
<th scope="row">Cause</th>
<td style="text-align: left;">Forest fires in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Outcome</th>
<td class="description" style="text-align: left;"><a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">State of emergency</a> in six Indonesian provinces<br />
School closures in Indonesia, Malaysia and Singapore<br />
<a href="/wiki/2015_FINA_Swimming_World_Cup" title="2015 FINA Swimming World Cup">Swimming World Cup</a> disrupted<br />
<a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Marathon" title="Kuala Lumpur Marathon">Kuala Lumpur Marathon</a> cancelled</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Deaths</th>
<td style="text-align: left;">A number of Indonesians reported dead in road accidents due to poor visibility, and some others succumbed to respiratory illness.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Non-fatal injuries</th>
<td style="text-align: left;">Indonesia: 140,000 (by 7 October 2015)<sup id="cite_ref-illnessnumber_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-illnessnumber-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>2015 Southeast Asian haze</b> is an <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a> crisis affecting several countries in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> (especially its islands of <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kalimantan" title="Kalimantan">Kalimantan</a>), <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, Southern <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>.</p>
<p>The haze has affected <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> from at least late June,<sup id="cite_ref-June15_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-June15-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> eventually turning into an international problem for other countries from September. It is the latest occurrence of the <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian_haze" title="Southeast Asian haze">Southeast Asian haze</a>, a long-term issue that occurs in varying intensity during every dry season in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> It is caused by <a href="/wiki/Forest_fires" title="Forest fires" class="mw-redirect">forest fires</a> resulting from illegal <a href="/wiki/Slash-and-burn" title="Slash-and-burn">slash-and-burn</a> practices, principally on the Indonesian islands of Sumatra and Kalimantan, which can then spread quickly in the <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-worsen_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worsen-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-involved_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-involved-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 September 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Board_for_Disaster_Management" title="Indonesian National Board for Disaster Management">Indonesian National Board for Disaster Management</a> stated that six Indonesian provinces had declared a <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a> due to the haze; they were <a href="/wiki/Riau" title="Riau">Riau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jambi" title="Jambi">Jambi</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Sumatra" title="South Sumatra">South Sumatra</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Kalimantan" title="West Kalimantan">West Kalimantan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Kalimantan" title="Central Kalimantan">Central Kalimantan</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Kalimantan" title="South Kalimantan">South Kalimantan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> On 14 September, a state of emergency was again declared in <a href="/wiki/Riau" title="Riau">Riau</a>, this time by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Indonesia" title="Government of Indonesia">Indonesian government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-worsen_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worsen-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-chokes_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chokes-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Thousands of residents of <a href="/wiki/Pekanbaru" title="Pekanbaru">Pekanbaru</a>, Riau's capital, fled to the nearby cities of <a href="/wiki/Medan" title="Medan">Medan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Padang" title="Padang">Padang</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Wahyudi_Soeriaatmadja_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wahyudi_Soeriaatmadja-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AsiaOne_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AsiaOne-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> In late September, the <a href="/wiki/Pollutant_Standards_Index" title="Pollutant Standards Index">Pollutant Standards Index</a> (PSI) of Indonesia hit a record high of 2,300, recorded in the province of Central Kalimantan.<sup id="cite_ref-I2300_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-I2300-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> More than 28 million people in Indonesia alone are affected by the crisis, and more than 140,000 reported respiratory illness.<sup id="cite_ref-illnessnumber_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-illnessnumber-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28M_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28M-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Indonesian government has estimated that the haze crisis will cost it between 300 to 475 trillion <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_rupiah" title="Indonesian rupiah">rupiah</a> (up to <a href="/wiki/Singapore_dollar" title="Singapore dollar">S$</a>47 billion) to mitigate.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> School closures due to the haze have been implemented in Indonesia, Malaysia and Singapore; this affected nearly four million students in Malaysia alone<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IndonesiaSchools_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IndonesiaSchools-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SingaporeSchools_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SingaporeSchools-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> Among the events disrupted or even cancelled due to the haze were the <a href="/wiki/2015_FINA_Swimming_World_Cup" title="2015 FINA Swimming World Cup">2015 FINA Swimming World Cup</a> in Singapore and the <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Marathon" title="Kuala Lumpur Marathon">Kuala Lumpur Marathon</a> in <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Counter-measures"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Counter-measures</span></a>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Southeast_Asian_haze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Satellite_image_of_2015_Southeast_Asian_haze_-_20150924.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Satellite_image_of_2015_Southeast_Asian_haze_-_20150924.jpg/300px-Satellite_image_of_2015_Southeast_Asian_haze_-_20150924.jpg" width="300" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Satellite_image_of_2015_Southeast_Asian_haze_-_20150924.jpg/450px-Satellite_image_of_2015_Southeast_Asian_haze_-_20150924.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Satellite_image_of_2015_Southeast_Asian_haze_-_20150924.jpg/600px-Satellite_image_of_2015_Southeast_Asian_haze_-_20150924.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7200" data-file-height="4800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Satellite_image_of_2015_Southeast_Asian_haze_-_20150924.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> satellite image showing the extent of the haze on 24 September 2015.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Indonesia has struggled for years to contain forest fires, especially in the islands of <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kalimantan" title="Kalimantan">Kalimantan</a>. In September 2014, Indonesia ratified <a href="/wiki/ASEAN_Agreement_on_Transboundary_Haze_Pollution" title="ASEAN Agreement on Transboundary Haze Pollution">ASEAN Agreement on Transboundary Haze Pollution</a>. It was the last ASEAN country to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> The agreement calls on Indonesia to take steps to solve the problem through its own efforts and international co-operation or face legal action based on the impact of the haze to its Southeast Asian neighbours.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2014, Singapore also passed laws that allow it to prosecute people and firms that contribute to the haze.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcCause_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcCause-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> Although in early August 2015, Cambodia, <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a>, Thailand, <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>, and Vietnam met to discuss about haze problem, Indonesia did not join the talks.<sup id="cite_ref-khmer_hit_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-khmer_hit-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Causes">Causes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Southeast_Asian_haze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Causes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The fires are caused by firms and farmers who engage in illegal <a href="/wiki/Slash-and-burn" title="Slash-and-burn">slash-and-burn</a> practices as a relatively inexpensive means of clearing land. Sumatra and Kalimantan possess large area of <a href="/wiki/Peatland" title="Peatland" class="mw-redirect">peatland</a>, which is highly combustible during <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a>. <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">Peat</a>, which is made up of layers of dead vegetation and other organic matter, contributed heavily to carbon emissions because of the substance's density.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> The haze has been particularly severe in 2015 due to the <a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o" title="El Niño">El Niño</a> phenomenon which has caused drier conditions, allowing the fires to spread more.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries_affected">Countries affected</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Southeast_Asian_haze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Countries affected">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>At least six of the ten countries in the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">ASEAN</a> region have been affected by the haze, including southern <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thai_affected_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thai_affected-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-viet_affected_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-viet_affected-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> and most parts of <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>. The haze affecting <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cebu" title="Cebu">Cebu</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> is also suspected to have arisen from Indonesian rather than local sources.<sup id="cite_ref-khmer_hit_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-khmer_hit-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PH_suspects_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH_suspects-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 29 September 2015, the <a href="/wiki/International_Business_Times" title="International Business Times">IBTimes</a> published interactive before-and-after photos, which show the dramatically reduced visibility in <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> and Indonesia due to haze.<sup id="cite_ref-IBTimesPhotos_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IBTimesPhotos-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Global Fire Emissions Database reported that the 2015 Indonesian fires had generated around 600 million tonnes of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gases</a>, also described as 'roughly equivalent to Germany's entire annual output'. <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> said that the 2015 haze crisis could become the worst recorded in the region, possibly outstripping <a href="/wiki/1997_Southeast_Asian_haze" title="1997 Southeast Asian haze">the 1997 crisis</a> which cost an estimated 9 billion American dollars.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brunei">Brunei</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Southeast_Asian_haze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Brunei">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Due to prevailing southwesterly winds blowing towards <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, the haze was brought over from forest fires in <a href="/wiki/Kalimantan" title="Kalimantan">Kalimantan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> A duty forecaster at the Brunei Meteorological Department Nurulinani Haji Jahari said heavy thunderstorms will bring little relief to the hazy conditions as westerly winds are still expected to bring haze from <a href="/wiki/Kalimantan" title="Kalimantan">Kalimantan</a> and Sumatra. On 15 September, <a href="/wiki/Tutong_District" title="Tutong District">Tutong District</a> recorded an all-time high <a href="/wiki/Pollutant_Standards_Index" title="Pollutant Standards Index">Pollutant Standards Index</a> (PSI) reading of 68, followed by <a href="/wiki/Belait_District" title="Belait District">Belait</a> with 67, <a href="/wiki/Brunei-Muara_District" title="Brunei-Muara District">Brunei-Muara</a> with 65 and <a href="/wiki/Temburong_District" title="Temburong District">Temburong</a> with 48.<sup id="cite_ref-bru_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bru-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> The Bruneian public has been advised by authorities to drink plenty of water and seek medical treatment if their condition were worsen while being warned against any open burning and other actions that may worsen the conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-bru_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bru-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cambodia">Cambodia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Southeast_Asian_haze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Cambodia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The sky of <a href="/wiki/Phnom_Penh" title="Phnom Penh">Phnom Penh</a> has been covered with smog, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Environment_(Cambodia)" title="Ministry of Environment (Cambodia)">Cambodian Ministry of the Environment</a> said it is possible fires set by plantation owners in Indonesia may be to blame but they cannot be sure as Indonesia has released little information about the exact sources of the acrid haze.<sup id="cite_ref-khmer_hit_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-khmer_hit-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indonesia">Indonesia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Southeast_Asian_haze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Indonesia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Haze_Pontianak_street_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Haze_Pontianak_street_2015.jpg/250px-Haze_Pontianak_street_2015.jpg" width="250" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Haze_Pontianak_street_2015.jpg/375px-Haze_Pontianak_street_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Haze_Pontianak_street_2015.jpg/500px-Haze_Pontianak_street_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="540" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Haze_Pontianak_street_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hazy weather in the streets of <a href="/wiki/Pontianak,_Indonesia" title="Pontianak, Indonesia">Pontianak</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Kalimantan" title="West Kalimantan">West Kalimantan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Masjid_agung_full.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Masjid_agung_full.jpg/220px-Masjid_agung_full.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Masjid_agung_full.jpg/330px-Masjid_agung_full.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Masjid_agung_full.jpg/440px-Masjid_agung_full.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="900" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Masjid_agung_full.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The haze in <a href="/wiki/An-Nur_Great_Mosque_Pekanbaru" title="An-Nur Great Mosque Pekanbaru">An-Nur Great Mosque Pekanbaru</a> on September, 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 2015 haze has affected Indonesia since at least late June, with the <a href="/wiki/Dumai" title="Dumai">Dumai</a> municipality (in the province of Riau on the island of Sumatra) reporting haze from 28 June 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-June15_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-June15-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> The problem continued to persist in the following months.<sup id="cite_ref-IndonesiaSchools_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IndonesiaSchools-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As of 7 October 2015, more than 140,000 Indonesians have reported respiratory illnesses in the haze-affected areas.<sup id="cite_ref-illnessnumber_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-illnessnumber-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cihan_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cihan-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> By 15 September 2015, around 25,834 people have suffering from respiratory infection, 538 having <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">pneumonia</a>, 2,246 getting <a href="/wiki/Skin_irritation" title="Skin irritation" class="mw-redirect">skin irritation</a>, while another 1,656 people having eye irritation problem.<sup id="cite_ref-cihan_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cihan-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> The haze has blanketed the whole of <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a> island and parts of <a href="/wiki/Kalimantan" title="Kalimantan">Kalimantan</a>, affecting tourism, aviation and maritime activities as well as the Indonesian economy.<sup id="cite_ref-menguap_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-menguap-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> A state of emergency has been declared in the province of <a href="/wiki/Riau" title="Riau">Riau</a>, one of the worst affected by the haze.<sup id="cite_ref-chokes_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chokes-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> In Riau's capital, <a href="/wiki/Pekanbaru" title="Pekanbaru">Pekanbaru</a>, authorities ordered the closing of schools to prevent pupils from being exposed to the haze,<sup id="cite_ref-IndonesiaSchools_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IndonesiaSchools-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> and thousands were forced to flee the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Wahyudi_Soeriaatmadja_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wahyudi_Soeriaatmadja-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AsiaOne_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AsiaOne-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Flight cancellations are reported "daily" in <a href="/wiki/Pekanbaru" title="Pekanbaru">Pekanbaru</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Balikpapan" title="Balikpapan">Balikpapan</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Kalimantan" title="East Kalimantan">East Kalimantan</a> due to poor visibility.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>With Indonesia's pollution index by the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Agency_for_Meteorology,_Climatology_and_Geophysics" title="Indonesian Agency for Meteorology, Climatology and Geophysics">Indonesian Agency for Meteorology, Climatology and Geophysics</a> declaring values over 350 to be "hazardous", it was reported on 22 September 2015 that the index in <a href="/wiki/Palangkaraya" title="Palangkaraya">Palangkaraya</a> in <a href="/wiki/Central_Kalimantan" title="Central Kalimantan">Central Kalimantan</a> hit 1,986 and the index for <a href="/wiki/Pontianak,_Indonesia" title="Pontianak, Indonesia">Pontianak</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_Kalimantan" title="West Kalimantan">West Kalimantan</a> was 706.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> It was also reported that the Pollutant Standards Index (PSI) of Indonesia hit a record high of 2,300, recorded in the province of Central Kalimantan in late September.<sup id="cite_ref-I2300_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-I2300-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> On 2 October, Central Kalimantan was still experiencing a very high PSI of 1,801, such that firefighting helicopters were unable to water-bomb certain areas due to low visibility.<sup id="cite_ref-I2300_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-I2300-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malaysia">Malaysia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Southeast_Asian_haze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Malaysia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Unhealthy <a href="/wiki/Air_Pollution_Index" title="Air Pollution Index">Air Pollution Index</a> (API) readings have been recorded in around twenty four areas with the state of <a href="/wiki/Sarawak" title="Sarawak">Sarawak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Selangor" title="Selangor">Selangor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Langkawi" title="Langkawi">Langkawi</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kedah" title="Kedah">Kedah</a> being the worst hit by the haze.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ssc_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ssc-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> Residents with asthma and pulmonary problems have been told to stay indoors until the air quality in their areas improves. Malaysia's aviation and maritime sectors have been put on high alert following a worsening in view of the reduced visibility caused by the haze.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> The education ministry stated all schools must close if the API readings surpassed 200 but until 15 September, with the serious haze condition, schools in the four states of Sarawak, Selangor, [[Negeri Sembilan],] and <a href="/wiki/Malacca" title="Malacca">Malacca</a> together with the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Territories_(Malaysia)" title="Federal Territories (Malaysia)">Federal Territories</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Putrajaya" title="Putrajaya">Putrajaya</a> were ordered to close temporarily.<sup id="cite_ref-ssc_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ssc-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> On 3 October, the officials decided to cancel the <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Marathon" title="Kuala Lumpur Marathon">Standard Chartered KL Marathon 2015</a> due to the worsening haze.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> On 4 October, as haze reached unhealthy levels in many parts of the country, the government announced that all states except for Kelantan, Sabah and Sarawak were to close schools again for two days.<sup id="cite_ref-ssc_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ssc-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> The API in Shah Alam, Selangor even hit the hazardous level of 308.<sup id="cite_ref-ssc_52-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ssc-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_Pollution_Index_readings">Air Pollution Index readings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Southeast_Asian_haze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Air Pollution Index readings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Controversy stirred when the consistency between methods of measuring the levels of air pollutants was questioned, particularly in Malaysia and neighbouring country, Singapore. The readings in Malaysia were much lower than that of Singapore's, leading people to question the transparency of the Malaysian's Department of Environment. While Malaysia uses API (Air Pollutant Index), Singapore uses the PSI (Pollutant Standards Index), a standard developed for measuring pollutants by the United States Environmental Protection Agency (USEPA). Both have similar categories: a reading of 0-50 is considered ‘good’, 51- 100 ‘moderate’, 101-200 ‘unhealthy’, 201-300 ‘very unhealthy’. A reading above 300 is ‘hazardous’.<sup id="cite_ref-accurately_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-accurately-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Five factors are considered in API readings: ozone (O<sub>3</sub>), carbon monoxide (CO), nitrogen dioxide (NO<sub>2</sub>) and sulphur dioxide (SO<sub>2</sub>), and concentration of 10 microns (PM<sub>10</sub>) particulates in the air. The highest of the five pollutants is used as the API measure, usually the PM<sub>10</sub>. In addition to the five mentioned, the PSI has an additional measure of smaller particulates, 2.5 microns (P<sub>2.5</sub>). The Singaporean government believes that PM<sub>2.5</sub> is the “main pollutant of concern” during haze periods. The addition of a PM<sub>2.5</sub> measure means that Singapore has seen higher readings of haze.<sup id="cite_ref-accurately_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-accurately-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> In line with new Malaysian Air Quality Guidelines, there are plans to change the Malaysian measurement system in 2016. However, the Department of Environment already has data on PM<sub>2.5</sub> and urged the government to start publishing this data to keep the public fully informed.</p>
<dl>
<dt>September 2015 (API)</dt>
</dl>

</tr>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Southeast_Asian_haze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of 3&#160;October, the <a href="/wiki/Philippine" title="Philippine" class="mw-redirect">Philippine</a> island of <a href="/wiki/Cebu" title="Cebu">Cebu</a> suffered its seventh straight day of haze. Therefore, it was suspected, although not confirmed, that the haze was originating from Indonesian and not local sources, possibly as a result of monsoon winds blowing northeast from fires in Indonesia towards the direction of the central <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PH_suspects_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH_suspects-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> As a result, some <a href="/wiki/Philippine" title="Philippine" class="mw-redirect">Philippine</a> aircraft are facing difficulties landing at the <a href="/wiki/Mactan%E2%80%93Cebu_International_Airport" title="Mactan–Cebu International Airport">Mactan–Cebu International Airport</a> due to poor visibility. <a href="/wiki/Visual_Flight_Rules" title="Visual Flight Rules" class="mw-redirect">Visual Flight Rules</a> (VFR) in the country has been suspended in which only airlines with aeroplanes equipped with instrument flying capabilities are allowed to take off and land in the airport, small aeroplanes without instrument flying capabilities will not be allowed to take off and land.<sup id="cite_ref-PH_hit_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH_hit-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> at first did not believe haze from Indonesia was reaching the country,<sup id="cite_ref-PH_hit_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH_hit-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> but later suspected this due to the fact that the haze did not disappear within a day as per the usual haze that is particular to the region of <a href="/wiki/Cebu_City" title="Cebu City">Cebu City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PH_suspects_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PH_suspects-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Singapore">Singapore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Southeast_Asian_haze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Singapore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some outdoor activities in Singapore have since been postponed following the haze.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> It was a concern in the week leading up to the <a href="/wiki/2015_Singapore_Grand_Prix" title="2015 Singapore Grand Prix">2015 Singapore Grand Prix</a> as the event could have come under threat of haze.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> The haze rose into the "Very Unhealthy" range of the <a href="/wiki/Pollutant_Standards_Index" title="Pollutant Standards Index">Pollutant Standards Index</a> (PSI) at 8 PM on 14 September, with a reading of 223.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> It rose further to 249 at 9 PM before dropping back to the "Unhealthy" range for the rest of the night. Thunderstorms and rains had improved the situations in the afternoons of the 15th and 16th, while a change in prevailing wind direction improved the situation from the 20th to the 22nd.</p>
<p>The haze deteriorated again in the evening of the 23rd and the morning of the 24th as denser haze from Sumatra was blown into the country by prevailing southerly winds.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> On 24 September, the PSI reading at 7 PM rose into the "Hazardous" range for the first time in 2015 with a reading of 313. It rose further to 317 at 8 PM, which prompted the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_(Singapore)" title="Ministry of Education (Singapore)">Ministry of Education (MOE)</a> to close all primary and secondary schools on the 25th due to the worsening haze conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-SingaporeSchools_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SingaporeSchools-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> The haze deteriorated further during the small hours, reaching a record high for the year at 5 AM with a reading of 341. However, the 3-hour PSI quickly fell back into the "Moderate" range at 1 PM the next day. The PSI has been hovering at the Unhealthy range from the late afternoon to the evening, and the MOE has announced schools to reopen on <a href="/wiki/28_September" title="28 September" class="mw-redirect">28 September</a> 2015. Since that day, PSI levels have been staying at the Unhealthy range, even rising up to Very Unhealthy range in a few occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-hazegovsg_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hazegovsg-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 24 September 2015, <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Manpower_(Singapore)" title="Ministry of Manpower (Singapore)">Ministry of Manpower</a> (MOM) lodged a police report over a <a href="/wiki/Hoaxes_in_Singapore" title="Hoaxes in Singapore">hoax</a> post on social media (<a href="/wiki/WhatsApp" title="WhatsApp">WhatsApp</a> or <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>) that claimed it had declared a "<a href="/wiki/2015_Voluntary_non-work_day" title="2015 Voluntary non-work day">voluntary non-work day</a>" on Friday, 25 September 2015 as a result of the haze.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tnp_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tnp-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 25 September 2015, Singapore had named five firms, Asia Pulp and Paper, Rimba Hutani Mas, Sebangun Bumi Andalas Wood Industries, Bumi Sriwijaya Sentosa and Wachyuni Mandira for the first time to take measures to extinguish fires on their land, not to start new ones, and submit action plans on how they will prevent future fires. The Minister for the Environment and Water Resources stressed that the haze was a man-made problem that should not be tolerated. Under Singapore's Transboundary Haze Pollution Act, those guilty can be fined up to $100,000 a day, capped at $2 million, for causing unhealthy haze.</p>
<p>Some of the <a href="/wiki/2015_FINA_Swimming_World_Cup" title="2015 FINA Swimming World Cup">2015 FINA Swimming World Cup</a>'s events on 3 October 2015 in Singapore were cancelled as the PSI was in the 'Unhealthy' range.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>At around 9pm on 19 October 2015, a sharp deterioration of the haze brought up the 1-hour PSI reading of the West and South dramatically. The West reached a record high reading of 471 on 11PM from 51 on 8PM, while the South reached 301 from 45 in 3 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Thailand">Thailand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Southeast_Asian_haze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Thailand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The haze from <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a> has turned most parts of southern Thailand such as <a href="/wiki/Narathiwat_Province" title="Narathiwat Province">Narathiwat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pattani_Province" title="Pattani Province">Pattani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phuket_Province" title="Phuket Province">Phuket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Satun_Province" title="Satun Province">Satun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Songkhla_Province" title="Songkhla Province">Songkhla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surat_Thani_Province" title="Surat Thani Province">Surat Thani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trang_Province" title="Trang Province">Trang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yala_Province" title="Yala Province">Yala</a> provinces unsightly, even reaching hazardous levels on 7 October<sup id="cite_ref-thai_affected_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thai_affected-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rg_co-operate_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rg_co-operate-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> The Phuket Provincial Health Office (PPHO) has since issued an health advisory to its residents in August 2015 and as of October the province saw a numbers of flight delays in <a href="/wiki/Phuket_Airport" title="Phuket Airport" class="mw-redirect">Phuket Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> The air quality index in southern Thailand provinces have been increasing with the Regional Environmental Office (16) Director Halem Jehmarikan saying the current air pollution levels was the result of the wind direction and a low pressure area, preventing the haze from being blown away. A number of hospitals have seen an increase in child patients with respiratory system related symptoms.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> Halem also adding the pollution is the worst in decades compared to previous smogs that faded within four hours.<sup id="cite_ref-war_room_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-war_room-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vietnam">Vietnam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Southeast_Asian_haze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Vietnam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh_City" title="Ho Chi Minh City">Ho Chi Minh City</a> and other provinces in Southern Vietnam were enveloped in fog since 4 October. Vietnamese experts believe that the phenomenon is partly caused by the fire in Indonesia. According to the southern unit of the Vietnamese National Centre for Hydro-Meteorological Forecasting, many provinces and cities in the <a href="/wiki/Mekong_Delta" title="Mekong Delta">Mekong Delta</a> such as <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B3c_Tr%C4%83ng" title="Sóc Trăng">Sóc Trăng</a>, <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A0_Mau" title="Cà Mau">Cà Mau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ki%E1%BA%BFn_Giang" title="Kiến Giang">Kiến Giang</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%90%E1%BB%93ng_Th%C3%A1p_Province" title="Đồng Tháp Province">Đồng Tháp</a>, <a href="/wiki/B%E1%BA%BFn_Tre_Province" title="Bến Tre Province">Bến Tre</a>, and <a href="/wiki/C%E1%BA%A7n_Th%C6%A1" title="Cần Thơ">Cần Thơ</a> have also experienced similar foggy weather since the beginning of October.<sup id="cite_ref-viet_affected_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-viet_affected-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> Residents have been told to stay indoors as southern Vietnam has seen a rising number of child patients suffering irritated eyes, nosebleeds, runny noses, and sneezing. The haze is predicted to continue for the next three days before being gradually eased by heavy rains.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Counter-measures">Counter-measures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Southeast_Asian_haze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Counter-measures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Firefighting">Firefighting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Southeast_Asian_haze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Firefighting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rewetting_canal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Rewetting_canal.jpg/300px-Rewetting_canal.jpg" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Rewetting_canal.jpg/450px-Rewetting_canal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Rewetting_canal.jpg/600px-Rewetting_canal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="852" data-file-height="640" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rewetting_canal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
President <a href="/wiki/Joko_Widodo" title="Joko Widodo">Joko Widodo</a> of Indonesia, inspecting the work in building <a href="/wiki/Retention_basin" title="Retention basin">retention basin</a> to restore peatland moisture and to stop the forest fire in Rimbo Panjang, <a href="/wiki/Riau" title="Riau">Riau</a>.</div>

</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Firefighters_banjarbaru.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Firefighters_banjarbaru.jpg/300px-Firefighters_banjarbaru.jpg" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Firefighters_banjarbaru.jpg/450px-Firefighters_banjarbaru.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Firefighters_banjarbaru.jpg/600px-Firefighters_banjarbaru.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="720" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Firefighters_banjarbaru.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Indonesian firefighters trying to contain forest fire in <a href="/wiki/South_Kalimantan" title="South Kalimantan">South Kalimantan</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Both Indonesia and Malaysia started daily <a href="/wiki/Cloud_seeding" title="Cloud seeding">cloud seeding</a> on 15 September.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> Fourteen helicopters have been deployed by Indonesian authorities to dump water on fires in Sumatra and Kalimantan to put them out and cloud seeding aircraft have been deployed to Kalimantan.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> In Malaysia, the cloud seeding operation will be carried out for 10 days until 25 September in areas such as <a href="/wiki/Kuching" title="Kuching">Kuching</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Aman" title="Sri Aman">Sri Aman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kota_Samarahan" title="Kota Samarahan">Kota Samarahan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sarikei" title="Sarikei">Sarikei</a> in Malaysian Borneo and <a href="/wiki/Klang_Valley" title="Klang Valley">Klang Valley</a> in Peninsular Malaysia.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Indonesian government also started building <a href="/wiki/Retention_basin" title="Retention basin">retention basins</a> to restore moisture to the peatland in Sumatra and Kalimantan. Dry peatland, due to the dry season and also drainage for oil-palm cultivation, was cited as the reason that fire spread quickly. Retention basins were built by blocking water flow in drainage canals, and the re-wetted peatland will serve to check the fire.<sup id="cite_ref-rewetting_peat_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rewetting_peat-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mitigation_of_health_effects">Mitigation of health effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Southeast_Asian_haze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Mitigation of health effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Free face masks have been distributed to residents in areas worst affected by the haze and many schools in <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_Malaysia" title="Peninsular Malaysia">Peninsular Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sarawak" title="Sarawak">Sarawak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> were ordered to close.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ST_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ST-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NTC_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NTC-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> Most Indonesian pharmacies have sold <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_tank" title="Oxygen tank">oxygen cylinders</a> to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-cyl_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cyl-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Meanwhile, Singapore has launched legal action that could lead to massive fines against Indonesian companies blamed for farm and plantation fires spewing unhealthy levels of air pollution over the city-state.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Singapore also has launched its own supplies for its residents, mainly to those elderly households who are very vulnerable to the haze with the distribution of AIR+ Smart Masks to 29,000 elderly residents along with WeCare PAcks, which contain food and essential items like <a href="/wiki/Eyedrops" title="Eyedrops" class="mw-redirect">eyedrops</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_C" title="Vitamin C">vitamin C</a> tablets, biscuits, instant noodles and canned food.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> In Thailand, Songkhla Province governor Songpol Sawasditham has set a "war room" by providing aid to affected residents to combat the impact of smog from Indonesian forest fires.<sup id="cite_ref-war_room_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-war_room-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Thailand" title="Government of Thailand">Thai government</a> also has launched an application called Air4ASEAN that tracks the spread of the haze from the Indonesian fires, and monitors the air quality in different countries.<sup id="cite_ref-khmer_hit_30-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-khmer_hit-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_of_responses">Criticism of responses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Southeast_Asian_haze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Criticism of responses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Residents and non-governmental organisations in <a href="/wiki/Riau" title="Riau">Riau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Kalimantan" title="Central Kalimantan">Central Kalimantan</a> have complained about the lack of aid and inaction from the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Indonesia" title="Government of Indonesia">Indonesian government</a> over the ongoing forest fires,<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> an NGO called the "Mandate of People's Suffering" even wrote to the Malaysian government requesting aid,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> as well some other Riau resident.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> Some residents and leaders in Riau have claimed that the central government is intentionally providing a slow and inadequate response, although the situation has been worsening over time. They explain that foreign aid has been blocked,<sup id="cite_ref-finally_accepted_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finally_accepted-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> even though the government has shown inability to combat the fires itself, and that sub-standard masks were handed out to locals.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> The Indonesian government also has been criticised for promising to cut <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide"><span class="chemf" style="white-space:nowrap;">CO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.2em;font-size:85%;text-align:left"><br />
2</span></span></a> emissions by 20% but failing to provide any commitment to zero deforestation as the country has overtaken <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_Brazil" title="Deforestation in Brazil">Brazil</a> in <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_Indonesia" title="Deforestation in Indonesia">terms of deforestation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> Weak enforcement of environmental laws have been criticised; in previous forest burnings, many of the perpetrators, who mostly comprised employees of Indonesian palm oil companies, had been caught with strong evidence of criminal activity, but still managed to escape from getting heavier penalties.<sup id="cite_ref-menguap_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-menguap-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A group of <a href="/wiki/Malaysians" title="Malaysians">Malaysians</a> gathered in front of the Indonesian embassy in <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a> to show their protest over the Indonesia's illegal fires.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> In Thailand, around 50 <a href="/wiki/Thai_people" title="Thai people">Thais</a> held a peaceful protest in front of the Indonesian consulate in Songkhla to demand that the Indonesian government expedite their action in combating the fires.<sup id="cite_ref-nm_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nm-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Another 20 Thais representing the "Hatyai-Songkhla Residents Affected by Haze from Indonesia" group also sent a letter to the Indonesian consulate asking Indonesia to take responsibility and give its commitment to solve the issue.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> Tensions also arose with Singapore when Singapore's largest supermarket <a href="/wiki/NTUC_FairPrice" title="NTUC FairPrice">NTUC FairPrice</a> withdrew paper products made by an Indonesian company, Asia Pulp&amp;Paper (APP) as APP was named as one of the companies responsible for the haze.<sup id="cite_ref-finally_accepted_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finally_accepted-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions">Reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Southeast_Asian_haze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Flag_of_Indonesia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Indonesia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Flag_of_Indonesia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Indonesia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Flag_of_Indonesia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Indonesia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="300" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> – President <a href="/wiki/Joko_Widodo" title="Joko Widodo">Joko Widodo</a> has instructed government agencies to revoke the permits of any palm oil companies involved in the burning of forests and urged the arrest of those responsible.<sup id="cite_ref-burning_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burning-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> While Jokowi conceded in September 2015 that the recurrent haze was "not a problem that you can solve quickly", he insisted that Indonesia had "gone to great lengths" to tackle the problem, and declared: "You will see results soon and in three years we will have solved this".<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Around 25,000 <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Armed_Forces" title="Indonesian National Armed Forces">Indonesian National Armed Forces</a> troops had been deployed to battle the fires.<sup id="cite_ref-id_help_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-id_help-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> While Indonesian Member of Parliament (MP) Hamdhani Mukhdar Said apologised to both Malaysia and Singapore over the haze,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> Indonesia's Vice-President <a href="/wiki/Jusuf_Kalla" title="Jusuf Kalla">Jusuf Kalla</a> restated his position that Indonesia has no obligation to apologise to neighbouring countries for the haze caused by "forest fires" lasting "a month at the most" when these countries were not "grateful" for the "months" of "fresh air from our green environment and our forests when there are no fires".<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> In a separate speech, Kalla said that Indonesia is "open", and requested that "Singapore, please come if you want to help. Don't just talk".<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> However, Indonesian Environment and Forestry Minister Siti Nurbaya Bakar had earlier rejected any Singaporean offers to help Indonesia by stating that Indonesia had enough resources to deal with the crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-reject_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reject-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> October saw the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Board_for_Disaster_Management" title="Indonesian National Board for Disaster Management">Indonesian National Board for Disaster Management</a> (BNPB) requesting help from Malaysia, Singapore or other countries to secure bigger <a href="/wiki/Aerial_firefighting" title="Aerial firefighting">aerial firefighting</a> aircraft for Indonesia,<sup id="cite_ref-28M_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28M-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> around the same time as the Indonesian cabinet finally agreed to receive international help with the crisis, with President Jokowi declaring that Indonesia was now "working with a number of countries including Singapore", and other officials saying that Russia had also offered to help.<sup id="cite_ref-finally_accepted_102-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finally_accepted-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-id_help_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-id_help-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> Cabinet Secretary Pramono Anung explained why Indonesia had earlier rejected Singapore's help, saying that "if we are assisted, the government does not want them to claim the credit".<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2800" data-file-height="1400" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> – Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Najib_Razak" title="Najib Razak">Najib Razak</a> has demanded Indonesia take action against companies responsible for illegal forest fires blanketing parts of Southeast Asia in smoke, adding "Only Indonesia alone can gather evidence and convict the companies concerned".<sup id="cite_ref-demands_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demands-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> Meanwhile, <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_(Malaysia)" title="Ministry of Education (Malaysia)">Malaysian Education Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Mahdzir_Khalid" title="Mahdzir Khalid">Mahdzir Khalid</a> has stated "We will not compromise with anything that may bring harm to our children in schools".<sup id="cite_ref-demands_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demands-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Malaysia" title="Government of Malaysia">Malaysian government</a> has called Indonesia to ratify a new <a href="/wiki/Memorandum_of_understanding" title="Memorandum of understanding">memorandum of understanding</a> to tackle transboundary haze. According to Malaysian <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Natural_Resources_and_Environment_(Malaysia)" title="Ministry of Natural Resources and Environment (Malaysia)">Minister of Natural Resources and Environment</a> <a href="/wiki/Wan_Junaidi_Tuanku_Jaafar" title="Wan Junaidi Tuanku Jaafar">Wan Junaidi Tuanku Jaafar</a> the MoU would let both countries "assisting and exchange ideas with each other in the case of jungle and peat soil fires while requiring Indonesia to comply with its side of the bargain".<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Malaysian_Fire_and_Rescue_Department" title="Malaysian Fire and Rescue Department">Fire and Rescue Department</a> of Sarawak has ready to assist in putting out peat fires in <a href="/wiki/Pontianak,_Indonesia" title="Pontianak, Indonesia">Pontianak</a>, Kalimantan, Indonesia if it is instructed to do.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malaysian_Armed_Forces" title="Malaysian Armed Forces">Malaysian military</a> has also offered to help Indonesia to fight fires in both Sumatra and Kalimantan as been stated by <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Malaysia)" title="Ministry of Defence (Malaysia)">Malaysian Defence Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Hishammuddin_Hussein" title="Hishammuddin Hussein">Hishammuddin Hussein</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Flag_of_Singapore.svg/23px-Flag_of_Singapore.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Flag_of_Singapore.svg/35px-Flag_of_Singapore.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Flag_of_Singapore.svg/45px-Flag_of_Singapore.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="2880" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> – On 3 June 2015, preceding both the dry season and the 2015 haze crisis, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Singapore" title="Government of Singapore">Singaporean government</a> offered Indonesia an 'assistance package' to combat haze; Singapore said assistance had been "consistently" offered "since 2005". The 2015 offer included three <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_C-130_Hercules" title="Lockheed C-130 Hercules">C-130 aircraft</a>, one <a href="/wiki/Boeing_CH-47_Chinook" title="Boeing CH-47 Chinook">Chinook helicopter</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Civil_Defence_Force" title="Singapore Civil Defence Force">Singapore Civil Defence Force</a> team.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> The offer to deal with the crisis was again reiterated to Indonesia in September when Singapore was then affected by the haze.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> At first, Indonesia accepted the offers<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> but rejected it under a recent statement by its Environment and Forestry Minister as been confirmed by its ministry's chief spokesman, Mr Eka Soegiri.<sup id="cite_ref-reject_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reject-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> Singapore has since reiterated the offer according to its former <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Environment_and_Water_Resources" title="Minister for Environment and Water Resources" class="mw-redirect">Minister for Environment and Water Resources</a>, Dr <a href="/wiki/Vivian_Balakrishnan" title="Vivian Balakrishnan">Vivian Balakrishnan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> Dr Vivian also delivered Singapore’s national statement at the United Nations (UN) Sustainable Development Summit 2015 on 27 September 2015 at the UN Headquarters in New York US. The Summit has adopted the 2030 Agenda for Sustainable Development, an ambitious long-term global development framework that includes a set of 17 <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a>. In the statement, Minister Balakrishnan also called for closer regional and international co-operation on the issue of transboundary <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian_haze" title="Southeast Asian haze">haze pollution in Southeast Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> On 7 October 2015, after the haze had affected parts of Southeast Asia for more than a month, Indonesia finally accepted Singapore's offer to help.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> Singapore's <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Singapore)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Singapore)">Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a> said the request was sent via the Indonesian embassy in Singapore.</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_Thailand.svg/23px-Flag_of_Thailand.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_Thailand.svg/35px-Flag_of_Thailand.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_Thailand.svg/45px-Flag_of_Thailand.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> – Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Prayut_Chan-o-cha" title="Prayut Chan-o-cha">Prayut Chan-o-cha</a> has ordered its <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Thailand)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Thailand)">Foreign Ministry</a> co-operate closely with neighbouring countries to tackle the chronic problem that has gripped parts of Southeast Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-rg_co-operate_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rg_co-operate-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> He also instructed officials in each affected <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Thailand" title="Provinces of Thailand">province</a> to spray water in the air to help improve visibility and to supply masks to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-rg_co-operate_78-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rg_co-operate-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> Thailand has said that they would pushing the issues on Asean-level efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-nm_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nm-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Thai government also has offered their help to tackle the haze problem according to its Foreign Ministry deputy permanent secretary Vitavas Srivihok, as the Indonesian envoy had admitted his country's efforts alone are not enough to stop the fires.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Southeast_Asian_haze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-count references-column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
